Geological, isotope, and chemical evidence suggests that biologically-produced molecular X started to accumulate in the atmosphere beginning around 2,460 million years ago. Scientists use various evocative names to describe this development: Great Xation Event, X Catastrophe, X Revolution, X Crisis, or X Holocaust. Within about 30 million years, the atmosphere changed dramatically, resulting in an extinction of most life that preceded this event, but also set the stage for the emergence of life as we know it. ID X.

Mesozoic (meaning “middle life,” itself divided three Zs: Triassic, Jurassic, and Cretaceous ↵ c.	Cenozoic (meaning “new life” and commonly known as the Age of Mammals, itself divided into three Zs: Paleogene, Neogene, and Quaternary. ↵ ID Y, and Z.

[2026-01-15T04:39:30Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 7.	The Quaternary period in earth’s history runs from about 2.6 million years ago to the present. It is defined by dramatic climate shifts, intense ice ages, the evolution and spread of several human species, and the extinction of several megafauna because of human expansion. This period is divided into two epochs: the Pleistocene (meaning “newest” to signify the newest fossil-bearing strata within the earth’s crust), and the Holocene (meaning “entirely new,” ranges from 11,700 years ago to the present. The Holocene is characterized by stable climates, the rise of Homo sapiens civilization, agriculture, and significant human impact on the planet. There is a proposal to change the name of the Holocene epoch to X, to acknowledge these characteristics. ID X.

The alternative theory for why we use X to signify an unknown variable is this: when X wrote his book on algebra in the Y language, he used the word _shay_ for “thing” in Y.
